and network activity.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;table&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Access Requests&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Tracks identity-based authentication events to determine which users accessed specific internal applications and whether those attempts were authorized.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Audit Logs&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Provides a trail of configuration changes within the Cloudflare dashboard to identify unauthorized administrative actions or modifications.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;CASB Findings&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Identifies security misconfigurations and data risks within SaaS applications (like Google Drive or Microsoft 365) to prevent unauthorized data exposure.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Magic Transit / IPSec Logs&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Helps network engineers perform network-level (L3) monitoring such as reviewing tunnel health and view BGP routing changes.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Browser Isolation Logs&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Tracks user actions &lt;i&gt;inside&lt;/i&gt; an isolated browser session (e.g., copy-paste, print, or file uploads) to prevent data leaks on untrusted sitesГӮВ &lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Device Posture ResultsГӮВ &lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Details the security health and compliance status of devices connecting to your network, helping to identify compromised or non-compliant endpoints.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;DEX Application TestsГӮВ &lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Monitors application performance from the user&amp;#39;s perspective, which can help distinguish between a security-related outage and a standard performance degradation.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;DEX Device State Events&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Provides telemetry on the physical state of user devices, useful for correlating hardware or OS-level anomalies with potential security incidents.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;DNS Firewall Logs&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Tracks DNS queries filtered through the DNS Firewall to identify communication with known malicious domains or command-and-control (C2) servers.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Email Security Alerts&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Logs malicious email activity and phishing attempts detected at the gateway to trace the origin of email-based entry vectors.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Gateway DNS&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Monitors every DNS query made by users on your network to identify shadow IT, malware callbacks, or domain-generation algorithms (DGAs).&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Gateway HTTP&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Provides full visibility into encrypted and unencrypted web traffic to detect hidden payloads, malicious file downloads, or unauthorized SaaS usage.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Gateway Network&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Tracks L3/L4 network traffic (non-HTTP) to identify unauthorized port usage, protocol anomalies, or lateral movement within the network.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;IPSec Logs&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Monitors the status and traffic of encrypted site-to-site tunnels to ensure the integrity and availability of secure network connections.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Magic IDS Detections&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Surfaces matches against intrusion detection signatures to alert investigators to known exploit patterns or malware behavior traversing the network.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Network Analytics Logs&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Provides high-level visibility into packet-level data to identify volumetric DDoS attacks or unusual traffic spikes targeting specific infrastructure.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Sinkhole HTTP Logs&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Captures traffic directed to &amp;quot;sinkholed&amp;quot; IP addresses to confirm which internal devices are attempting to communicate with known botnet infrastructure.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;WARP Config Changes&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Tracks modifications to the WARP client settings on end-user devices to ensure that security agents haven&amp;#39;t been tampered with or disabled.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;WARP Toggle Changes&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Specifically logs when users enable or disable their secure connectivity, helping to identify periods where a device may have been unprotected.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Zero Trust Network Session Logs&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Logs the duration and status of Events&lt;/b&gt;, and &lt;b&gt;DNS logs&lt;/b&gt; to see exactly how traffic is hitting your public-facing properties.&lt;b&gt; &lt;/b&gt;Track internal movement with &lt;b&gt;Access If a credential is compromised, youГўВҖВҷll see where they went. Use &lt;b&gt;Magic IDS&lt;/b&gt; and &lt;b&gt;Network Analytics logs&lt;/b&gt; to spot volumetric attacks and &amp;quot;East-West&amp;quot; lateral movement within your private network.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;identify-the-reconnaissance\&quot;&gt;Identify the reconnaissance&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#identify-the-reconnaissance\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;Attackers use scanners and other tools to look for entry points, hidden directories, or software vulnerabilities. To identify this, using Log Explorer, you can query &lt;code&gt;http_requests&lt;/code&gt; for any &lt;code&gt;EdgeResponseStatus&lt;/code&gt; codes of 401, 403, or 404 coming from a single IP, or requests to sensitive paths (e.g. &lt;code&gt;/.env&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;code&gt;/.git&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;code&gt;/wp-admin&lt;/code&gt;).ГӮВ &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Additionally, &lt;code&gt;magic_ids_detections&lt;/code&gt; logs can also be used to identify scanning at the network layer. These logs provide packet-level visibility into threats targeting your network. Unlike standard HTTP logs, these logs focus on &lt;b&gt;signature-based detections&lt;/b&gt; at the network and transport layers (IP, TCP, UDP). Query to discover cases where a single &lt;code&gt;SourceIP&lt;/code&gt; is triggering multiple unique detections across a wide range of &lt;code&gt;DestinationPort&lt;/code&gt; values in a short timeframe. Magic IDS signatures can specifically flag activities like Nmap scans or SYN stealth scans.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;check-for-diversions\&quot;&gt;Check for diversions&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#check-for-diversions\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;While the attacker is conducting reconnaissance, they may attempt to disguise this with a simultaneous network flood. Pivot to &lt;code&gt;network_analytics_logs&lt;/code&gt; to see if a volumetric attack is being used as a smokescreen.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;identify-the-approach\&quot;&gt;Identify the approachГӮВ &lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#identify-the-approach\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;Once attackers identify a potential vulnerability, they begin to craft their weapon. The attacker sends malicious payloads (e.g. SQL injection or large/corrupt file uploads) to confirm the vulnerability. Review &lt;code&gt;http_requests&lt;/code&gt; and/or &lt;code&gt;fw_events&lt;/code&gt; to identify any Cloudflare detection tools that have triggered. Cloudflare logs security signals in these datasets to easily identify requests with malicious payloads using fields such as &lt;code&gt;WAFAttackScore&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;code&gt;WAFSQLiAttackScore&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;code&gt;FraudAttack&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;code&gt;ContentScanJobResults&lt;/code&gt;, and several more. Review &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/logs/logpush/logpush-job/datasets/zone/http_requests/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;our documentation&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; to get a full understanding of these fields. The &lt;code&gt;fw_events&lt;/code&gt; logs can be used to determine whether these requests made it past CloudflareГўВҖВҷs defenses by examining the &lt;code&gt;action&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;code&gt;source&lt;/code&gt;, and &lt;code&gt;ruleID&lt;/code&gt; fields. CloudflareГўВҖВҷs managed rules by default blocks many of these payloads by default. Review Application Security Overview to know if your application is protected.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/1zpFguYrnbOPwyASGQCqZK/63f398acce2226e453a5eea1cc749241/image3.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;Showing the Managed rules Insight that displays on Security Overview if the current zone does not have Managed Rules enabled\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1117\&quot; height=\&quot;124\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;sup&gt;&lt;i&gt;Showing the Managed rules Insight that displays on Security Overview if the current zone does not have Managed Rules enabled&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;audit-the-identity\&quot;&gt;Audit the identity&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#audit-the-identity\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;Did that suspicious IP manage to log in? Use the &lt;code&gt;ClientIP&lt;/code&gt; to search &lt;code&gt;access_requests&lt;/code&gt;. If you see a &amp;quot;&lt;code&gt;Decision: Allow&lt;/code&gt;&amp;quot; for a sensitive internal app, you know you have a compromised account.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;stop-the-leak-data-exfiltration\&quot;&gt;Stop the leak (data exfiltration)&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#stop-the-leak-data-exfiltration\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;Attackers sometimes use DNS tunneling to bypass firewalls by encoding sensitive data (like passwords or SSH keys) into DNS queries. Instead of a normal request like &lt;code&gt;google.com&lt;/code&gt;, the logs will show long, encoded strings. Look for an unusually high volume of queries for unique, long, and high-entropy subdomains by examining the fields: &lt;code&gt;QueryName&lt;/code&gt;: Look for strings like &lt;a href=\&quot;http://h3ldo293js92.example.com\&quot;&gt;&lt;code&gt;&lt;u&gt;h3ldo293js92.example.com&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;code&gt;QueryType&lt;/code&gt;: Often uses &lt;code&gt;TXT&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;code&gt;CNAME&lt;/code&gt;, or &lt;code&gt;NULL&lt;/code&gt; records to carry the payload, and &lt;code&gt;ClientIP&lt;/code&gt;: Identify if a single internal host is generating thousands of these unique requests.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Additionally, attackers may attempt to leak sensitive data by hiding it within non-standard protocols or by using common protocols (like DNS or ICMP) in unusual ways to bypass standard firewalls. Discover this by querying the &lt;code&gt;magic_ids_detections&lt;/code&gt; logs to look for signatures that flag protocol anomalies, such as &amp;quot;ICMP tunneling&amp;quot; or &amp;quot;DNS tunneling&amp;quot; detections in the &lt;code&gt;SignatureMessage&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Whether you are investigating a zero-day vulnerability or tracking a sophisticated botnet, the data you need is now at your fingertips.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h2 id=\&quot;correlate-across-datasets\&quot;&gt;Correlate across datasets&lt;/h2&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#correlate-across-datasets\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;Investigate malicious activity across multiple datasets by pivoting between multiple concurrent searches. With Log Explorer, you can now work with multiple queries simultaneously with the new Tabs feature. Switch between tabs to query different datasets or Pivot and adjust queries using filtering via your query results.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;div style=\&quot;position: relative; padding-top: 45.348837209302324%;\&quot;&gt;\n  &lt;iframe\n    src=\&quot;https://customer-eq7kiuol0tk9chox.cloudflarestream.com/fdce57563737015fcb27147c4b44ac70/iframe?muted=true&amp;preload=true&amp;loop=true&amp;autoplay=true&amp;poster=https%3A%2F%2Fcustomer-eq7kiuol0tk9chox.cloudflarestream.com%2Ffdce57563737015fcb27147c4b44ac70%2Fthumbnails%2Fthumbnail.jpg%3Ftime%3D%26height%3D600\&quot;\n    loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;\n    style=\&quot;border: none; position: absolute; top: 0; left: 0; height: 100%; width: 100%;\&quot;\n    allow=\&quot;accelerometer; gyroscope; autoplay; encrypted-media; picture-in-picture;\&quot;\n    allowfullscreen=\&quot;true\&quot;\n  &gt;&lt;/iframe&gt;\n&lt;/div&gt;\n&lt;p&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;When you correlate data across multiple Cloudflare log sources, you can detect sophisticated multi-stage attacks that appear benign when viewed in isolation. This cross-dataset analysis allows you to see the full attack chain from reconnaissance to exfiltration.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;session-hijacking-token-theft\&quot;&gt;Session hijacking (token theft)&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#session-hijacking-token-theft\&quot; A user authenticates via Cloudflare Access, but their subsequent HTTP_request traffic looks like a bot.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Step 1:&lt;/b&gt; Identify high-risk sessions in &lt;code&gt;http_requests&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-SQL\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-SQL\&quot;&gt;SELECT RayID, ClientIP, ClientRequestUserAgent, BotScore\nFROM http_requests\nWHERE date = &amp;#039;2026-02-22&amp;#039; \n  AND BotScore &amp;lt; 20 \nLIMIT 100&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            &lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Step 2:&lt;/b&gt; Copy the &lt;code&gt;RayID&lt;/code&gt; and search &lt;code&gt;access_requests&lt;/code&gt; to see which user account is associated with that suspicious bot activity.&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-SQL\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-SQL\&quot;&gt;\nSELECT Email, IPAddress, Allowed\nFROM access_requests\nWHERE date = &amp;#039;2026-02-22&amp;#039; \n  AND RayID = &amp;#039;INSERT_RAY_ID_HERE&amp;#039;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            \n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;post-phishing-c2-beaconing\&quot;&gt;Post-phishing C2 beaconing&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#post-phishing-c2-beaconing\&quot; An employee clicked a link in a phishing email which resulted in compromising their workstation. This workstation sends a DNS query for a known malicious domain, then immediately triggers an IDS alert.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Step 1:&lt;/b&gt; Find phishing attacks by examining email_security_alerts for violations.ГӮВ &lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-SQL\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-SQL\&quot;&gt;SELECT Timestamp, Threatcategories, To, Alertreason\nFROM email_security_alerts\nWHERE date = &amp;#039;2026-02-22&amp;#039; \n  AND Threatcategories LIKE &amp;#039;phishing&amp;#039;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            &lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Step 2:&lt;/b&gt; Use Access logs to correlate the userГўВҖВҷs email (To) to their IP Address.&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-SQL\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-SQL\&quot;&gt;SELECT Email, IPAddress\nFROM access_requests\nWHERE date = &amp;#039;2026-02-22&amp;#039; &lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            &lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Step 3:&lt;/b&gt; Find internal IPs querying a specific malicious domain in &lt;code&gt;gateway_dns&lt;/code&gt; logs.&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-SQL\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-SQL\&quot;&gt;\nSELECT SrcIP, QueryName, DstIP, \nFROM gateway_dns\nWHERE date = &amp;#039;2026-02-22&amp;#039; \n  AND SrcIP = &amp;#039;INSERT_IP_FROM_PREVIOUS_QUERY&amp;#039;\n  AND QueryName LIKE &amp;#039;%malicious_domain_name%&amp;#039;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            \n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;lateral-movement-access-network-probing\&quot;&gt;Lateral movement (Access ГўВҶВ’ network probing)&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#lateral-movement-access-network-probing\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Scenario:&lt;/b&gt; A user logs in via Zero Trust and then tries to scan the internal network.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Step 1:&lt;/b&gt; Find successful logins from unexpected locations in &lt;code&gt;access_requests&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-SQL\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-SQL\&quot;&gt;SELECT IPAddress, Email, Country\nFROM access_requests\nWHERE date = &amp;#039;2026-02-22&amp;#039; \n  AND Allowed = true \n  AND Country != &amp;#039;US&amp;#039; -- Replace with your HQ country&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            &lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Step 2:&lt;/b&gt; Check if that &lt;code&gt;IPAddress&lt;/code&gt; is triggering network-level signatures in &lt;code&gt;magic_ids_detections&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-SQL\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-SQL\&quot;&gt;SELECT SignatureMessage, DestinationIP, Protocol\nFROM magic_ids_detections\nWHERE date = &amp;#039;2026-02-22&amp;#039; \n  AND SourceIP = &amp;#039;INSERT_IP_ADDRESS_HERE&amp;#039;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            \n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;opening-doors-for-more-data\&quot;&gt;Opening doors for more dataГӮВ &lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#opening-doors-for-more-data\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;From the beginning, Log Explorer was designed with extensibility in mind. Every dataset schema is defined using JSON Schema, a widely-adopted standard for describing the structure and types of JSON data. This design decision has enabled us to easily expand beyond HTTP Requests and Firewall Events to the full breadth of Cloudflare&amp;#39;s telemetry. The same schema-driven approach that powered our initial datasets scaled naturally to accommodate Zero Trust logs, network analytics, email security alerts, and everything in between.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;More importantly, this standardization opens the door to ingesting data beyond Cloudflare&amp;#39;s native telemetry. Because our ingestion pipeline is schema-driven rather than hard-coded, we&amp;#39;re positioned to accept any structured data that can be expressed in JSON format. For security teams managing hybrid environments, this means Log Explorer could eventually serve as a single pane of glass, correlating Cloudflare&amp;#39;s edge telemetry with logs from third-party sources, all queryable through the same SQL interface. While today&amp;#39;s release focuses on completing coverage of Cloudflare&amp;#39;s product portfolio, the architectural groundwork is laid for a future where customers can bring their own data sources with custom schemas.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;faster-data-faster-response-architectural-upgrades\&quot;&gt;Faster data, faster response: architectural upgrades&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#faster-data-faster-response-architectural-upgrades\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;To investigate a multi-vector attack effectively, timing is everything. A delay of even a few minutes in the log availability can be the difference between proactive defense and reactive damage control.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;That is why we have optimized our ingestion for better speed and resilience. By increasing concurrency in one part of our ingestion path, we have eliminated bottlenecks that could cause ГўВҖВңnoisy neighborГўВҖВқ issues, ensuring that one clientГўВҖВҷs data surge doesnГўВҖВҷt slow down anotherГўВҖВҷs visibility. This architectural work has reduced our P99 ingestion latency by approximately 55%, and our P50 by 25%, cutting the time it takes for an event at the edge to become available for your SQL queries.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/41M2eWP0BwrQFSZW4GzZbV/7a6139354abb561aba17e77d83beb17a/image4.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;Grafana chart displaying the drop in ingest latency after architectural upgrades\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1999\&quot; height=\&quot;882\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;sup&gt;&lt;i&gt;Grafana chart displaying the drop in ingest latency after architectural upgrades&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h2 id=\&quot;follow-along-for-more-updates\&quot;&gt;Follow along for more updates&lt;/h2&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#follow-along-for-more-updates\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;We&amp;#39;re just getting started. We&amp;#39;re actively working on even more powerful features to further enhance your experience with Log Explorer, including the ability to run these detection queries on a custom defined schedule.ГӮВ &lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/2JIOu9PXDwVAVcmbgq456q/1eace4b5d38bb705e82442a4ee8045dc/Scheduled_Queries_List.png\&quot; and keep an eye out for more Log Explorer updates soon in our &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/changelog/product/log-explorer/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Change Log&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.ГӮВ &lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h2 id=\&quot;get-access-to-log-explorer\&quot;&gt;Get access to Log Explorer&lt;/h2&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#get-access-to-log-explorer\&quot; Page for Locale&quot;]}],&quot;url&quot;:[0,&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/investigating-multi-vector-attacks-in-log-explorer&quot;],&quot;metadata&quot;:[0,{&quot;title&quot;:[0,&quot;Investigating multi-vector attacks in Log Explorer&quot;],&quot;description&quot;:[0,&quot;Log Explorer customers can now identify and investigate multi-vector attacks. Log Explorer supports 14 additional Cloudflare datasets, enabling users to have a 360-degree view of their network.&quot;],&quot;imgPreview&quot;:[0,&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/Vwu9ot7fM9tlU40L4aW1Z/184c881e42199453c8f7441c5cb0c35d/Investigating_multi-vector_attacks_in_Log_Explorer-OG.png&quot;]}],&quot;publicly_index&quot;:[0,true]}],[0,{&quot;id&quot;:[0,&quot;7yIVIjWT0unNpdtbhOCVnh&quot;],&quot;title&quot;:[0,&quot;Active defense: introducing a stateful vulnerability scanner for APIs&quot;],&quot;slug&quot;:[0,&quot;vulnerability-scanner&quot;],&quot;excerpt&quot;:[0,&quot;CloudflareГўВҖВҷs new Web and API Vulnerability Scanner helps teams proactively find logic flaws. By using AI to build API call graphs, we identify vulnerabilities that standard defensive tools miss.&quot;],&quot;featured&quot;:[0,false],&quot;html&quot;:[0,&quot;&lt;p&gt;Security is traditionally a game of defense. You build walls, set up gates, and write rules to block traffic that looks suspicious. For years, Cloudflare has been a leader in this space: our &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/application-services/products/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Application Security platform&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; is designed to catch attacks in flight, dropping malicious requests at the edge before they ever reach your origin. But for &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/learning/security/api/what-is-api-security/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;API security&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, defensive posturing isnГўВҖВҷt enough.ГӮВ &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;ThatГўВҖВҷs why today, we are launching the beta of CloudflareГўВҖВҷs Web and API Vulnerability Scanner.ГӮВ &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;We are starting with the most pervasive and difficult-to-catch threat on the OWASP API Top 10: &lt;a href=\&quot;https://owasp.org/API-Security/editions/2023/en/0xa1-broken-object-level-authorization/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Broken Object Level Authorization&lt;/u&gt;, or BOLA.&lt;/a&gt; We will add more vulnerability scan types over time, including both API and web application threats.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The most dangerous API vulnerabilities today arenГўВҖВҷt generic injection attacks or malformed requests that a WAF can easily spot. They are logic flawsГўВҖВ”perfectly valid HTTP requests that meet the protocol and application spec but defy the business logic.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;To find these, you canГўВҖВҷt just wait for an attack. You have to actively hunt for them.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The Web and API Vulnerability Scanner will be available first for &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/api-shield/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;API Shield&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; customers. Read on to learn why we are focused on API security scans for this first release.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h2 id=\&quot;why-purely-defensive-security-misses-the-mark\&quot;&gt;Why purely defensive security misses the mark&lt;/h2&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#why-purely-defensive-security-misses-the-mark\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;In the web application world, vulnerabilities often look like syntax errors. A &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/learning/security/threats/sql-injection/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;SQL injection&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; attempt looks like code where data should be. A &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/learning/security/threats/cross-site-scripting/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;cross-site scripting (XSS)&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; attack looks like a script tag in a form field. These have signatures.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;API vulnerabilities are different. To illustrate, letГўВҖВҷs imagine a food delivery mobile app that communicates solely with an API on the backend. LetГўВҖВҷs take the orders endpoint:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Endpoint Definition: &lt;/b&gt;&lt;code&gt;&lt;b&gt;/api/v1/orders&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;table&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Method&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Resource Path&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Description&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;GET&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;/api/v1/orders/{order_id}&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Check Status.&lt;/b&gt; Returns the tracking status of a specific order (e.g., &amp;quot;Kitchen is preparing&amp;quot;).&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;PATCH&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;/api/v1/orders/{order_id}&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Update Order.&lt;/b&gt; Allows the user to modify the drop-off location or add delivery instructions.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;p&gt;In a broken authorization attack like BOLA, User A (the attacker) requests to update the delivery address of a paid-for order belonging to User B (the victim). The attacker simply inserts User BГўВҖВҷs &lt;code&gt;{order_id}&lt;/code&gt; in the &lt;code&gt;PATCH&lt;/code&gt; request.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Here is what that request looks like, with ГўВҖВҳ8821ГўВҖВҷ as User BГўВҖВҷs order ID. Notice that User A is fully authenticated with their own valid token:&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-javascript\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-javascript\&quot;&gt;PATCH /api/v1/orders/8821 HTTP/1.1\nHost: api.example.com\nAuthorization: Bearer &amp;lt;User_A_Valid_Token&amp;gt;\nContent-Type: application/json\n\n{\n  &amp;quot;delivery_address&amp;quot;: &amp;quot;123 Attacker Way, Apt 4&amp;quot;,\n  &amp;quot;instructions&amp;quot;: &amp;quot;Leave at front door, ring bell&amp;quot;\n}\n&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            &lt;p&gt;The request headers are valid. The authentication token is valid. The schema is correct. To a standard WAF, this request looks perfect. A bot management offering may even be fooled if a human is manually sending the attack requests.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;User A will now get BГўВҖВҷs food delivered to them! The vulnerability exists because the API endpoint fails to validate if User A actually has permission to view or update user BГўВҖВҷs data. This is a failure of logic, not syntax. To fix this, the API developer could implement a simple check: &lt;code&gt;if (order.userID != user.ID) throw Unauthorized;&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/ZOOAjAYcZqzDYg9snYASL/65940a740ba7ef294b719e76d37f3cdd/BLOG-3161_2.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;BLOG-3161 2\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1728\&quot; height=\&quot;1428\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;You can detect these types of vulnerabilities by actively sending API test traffic or passively listening to existing API traffic. Finding these vulnerabilities through passive scanning requires context. Last year &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/changelog/2025-11-12-bola-attack-detection/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;we launched BOLA vulnerability detection&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; for API Shield. This detection automatically finds these vulnerabilities by passively scanning customer traffic for usage anomalies. To be successful with this type of scanning, you need to know what a &amp;quot;valid&amp;quot; API call looks like, what the variable parameters are, how a typical user behaves, and how the API behaves when those parameters are manipulated.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Yet there are reasons security teams may not have any of that context, even with access to API ShieldГўВҖВҷs BOLA vulnerability detection. Development environments may need to be tested but lack user traffic. Production environments may (thankfully) have a lack of attack traffic yet still need analysis, and so on. In these circumstances, and to be proactive in general, teams can turn to Dynamic Application Security Testing (DAST). By creating net-new traffic profiles intended specifically for security testing, DAST tools can look for vulnerabilities in any environment at any time.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Unfortunately, traditional DAST tools have a high barrier to entry. They are often difficult to configure, require you to manually upload and maintain Swagger/OpenAPI files, struggle to authenticate correctly against modern complex login flows, and can simply lack any API-specific security tests (e.g. BOLA).&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h2 id=\&quot;cloudflares-api-scanning-advantage\&quot;&gt;CloudflareГўВҖВҷs API scanning advantage&lt;/h2&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#cloudflares-api-scanning-advantage\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;In the food delivery order example above, we assumed the attacker could find a valid order to modify. While there are often avenues for attackers to gather this type of intelligence in a live production environment, in a security testing exercise you must create your own objects before testing the APIГўВҖВҷs authorization controls. For typical DAST scans, this can be a problem, because many scanners treat each individual request on its own. This method fails to chain requests together in the logical pattern necessary to find broken authorization vulnerabilities. Legacy DAST scanners can also exist as an island within your security tooling and orchestration environment, preventing their findings from being shared or viewed in context.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Vulnerability scanning from Cloudflare is different for a few key reasons.ГӮВ &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;First, &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/security-center/security-insights/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Security Insights&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; will list results from our new scans alongside any existing Cloudflare security findings for added context. YouГўВҖВҷll see all your posture management information in one place.ГӮВ &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Second,&lt;b&gt; &lt;/b&gt;we already know your APIГўВҖВҷs inputs and outputs. If you are an API Shield customer, Cloudflare already understands your API. Our &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/api-shield/security/api-discovery/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;API Discovery&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/api-shield/management-and-monitoring/endpoint-management/schema-learning/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Schema Learning&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; features passively catalog your endpoints and learn your traffic patterns. While youГўВҖВҷll need to manually upload an OpenAPI spec to get started for our initial release, you will be able to get started quickly without one in a future release.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Third, because we sit at the edge, we can turn passive traffic inspection knowledge into active intelligence. It will be easy to verify BOLA vulnerability detection risks (found via traffic inspection) by sending net-new HTTP requests with the vulnerability scanner.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;And finally, we have built a new, stateful DAST platform, as we detail below. Most scanners require hours of setup to &amp;quot;teach&amp;quot; the tool how to talk to your API. With Cloudflare, you can effectively skip that step and get started quickly. You provide the API credentials, and weГўВҖВҷll use your API schemas to automatically construct a scan plan.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h2 id=\&quot;building-automatic-scan-plans\&quot;&gt;Building automatic scan plans&lt;/h2&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#building-automatic-scan-plans\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;APIs are commonly documented using &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.openapis.org/what-is-openapi\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;OpenAPI schemas&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. These schemas denote the host, method, and path (commonly, an ГўВҖВңendpointГўВҖВқ) along with the expected parameters of incoming requests and resulting responses. In order to automatically build a scan plan, we must first make sense of these API specifications for any given API to be scanned.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Our scanner works by building up an API call graph from an OpenAPI document and subsequently walking it, using attacker and owner contexts. Owners create resources, attackers subsequently try to access them. Attackers are fully authenticated with their own set of valid credentials. If an attacker successfully reads, modifies or deletes an unowned resource, an authorization vulnerability is found.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Consider for example the above delivery order with ID 8821. For the server-side resource to exist, it needed to be originally created by an owner, most likely in a ГўВҖВңgenesisГўВҖВқ &lt;code&gt;POST&lt;/code&gt; request with no or minimal dependencies (previous necessary calls and resulting data). Modelling the API as a call graph, such an endpoint constitutes a node with no or few incoming edges (dependencies). Any subsequent request, such as the attackerГўВҖВҷs &lt;code&gt;PATCH&lt;/code&gt; above, then has a &lt;i&gt;data dependency&lt;/i&gt; (the data is &lt;code&gt;order_id&lt;/code&gt;) on the genesis request (the &lt;code&gt;POST&lt;/code&gt;). Without all data provided, the &lt;code&gt;PATCH&lt;/code&gt; cannot proceed.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/7q0y7XZJE411gzhRuo9UjG/f7722c58e6cac751a1db44b612098a7b/BLOG-3161_3.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;BLOG-3161 3\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1176\&quot; height=\&quot;1642\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;Here we see in purple arrows the nodes in this API graph that are necessary to visit to add a note to an order via the POST &lt;code&gt;/api/v1/orders/{order_id}/note/{note_id}&lt;/code&gt; endpoint. &lt;b&gt;Importantly, none of the steps or logic shown in the diagram is available in the OpenAPI specification!&lt;/b&gt; It must be inferred logically through some other means, and that is exactly what our vulnerability scanner will do automatically.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;In order to reliably and automatically plan scans across a variety of APIs, we must accurately model these endpoint relationships from scratch. However, two problems arise: data quality of API specifications is not guaranteed, and even functionally complete schemas can have ambiguous naming schemes. Consider a simplified OpenAPI specification for the above API, which might look like&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-javascript\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-javascript\&quot;&gt;openapi: 3.0.0\ninfo:\n  title: Order API\n  version: 1.0.0\npaths:\n  /api/v1/orders:\n    post:\n      summary: Create an order\n      requestBody:\n        required: true\n        content:\n          application/json:\n            schema:\n              type: object\n              properties:\n                product:\n                  type: string\n                count:\n                  type: integer\n              required:\n                - product\n                - count\n      responses:\n        &amp;#039;201&amp;#039;:\n          description: Item created successfully\n          content:\n            application/json:\n              schema:\n                type: object\n                properties:\n                  result:\n                    type: object\n                    properties:\n                      id:\n                        type: integer\n                      created_at:\n                        type: integer\n                  errors:\n                    type: array\n                    items:\n                      type: string\n  /api/v1/orders/{order_id}:\n    patch:\n      summary: Modify an order by ID\n      parameters:\n        - name: order_id\n          in: path\n&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            &lt;p&gt;We can see that the &lt;code&gt;POST&lt;/code&gt; endpoint returns responses such as&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-json\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-json\&quot;&gt;{\n    &amp;quot;result&amp;quot;: {\n        &amp;quot;id&amp;quot;: 8821,\n        &amp;quot;created_at&amp;quot;: 1741476777\n    },\n   &amp;quot;errors&amp;quot;: []\n}\n&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            &lt;p&gt;To a human observer, it is quickly evident that &lt;code&gt;$.result.id&lt;/code&gt; is the value to be injected in &lt;code&gt;order_id&lt;/code&gt; for the &lt;code&gt;PATCH&lt;/code&gt; endpoint. The &lt;code&gt;id&lt;/code&gt; property might also be called &lt;code&gt;orderId, value&lt;/code&gt; or something else, and be nested arbitrarily. These subtle inconsistencies in OpenAPI documents of arbitrary shape are intractable for heuristics-based approaches.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Our scanner uses CloudflareГўВҖВҷs own &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/workers-ai/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Workers AI&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; platform to tackle this fuzzy problem space. Models such as &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/workers-ai/models/gpt-oss-120b/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;OpenAIГўВҖВҷs open-weight gpt-oss-120b&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; are powerful enough to match data dependencies reliably, and to generate realistic fake&lt;i&gt; &lt;/i&gt;data where necessary, essentially filling in the blanks of OpenAPI specifications. Leveraging &lt;a href=\&quot;https://platform.openai.com/docs/guides/structured-outputs\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;structured outputs&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, the model produces a representation of the API call graph for our scanner to walk, injecting attacker and owner credentials appropriately.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;This approach tackles the problem of needing human intelligence to infer authorization and data relationships in OpenAPI schemas with artificial intelligence to do the same. Structured outputs bridge the gap from the natural language world of gpt-oss back to machine-executable instructions. In addition to Workers AI solving the planning problem, self-hosting on Workers AI means our system automatically benefits from CloudflareГўВҖВҷs highly available, globally distributed architecture.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;built-on-proven-foundations\&quot;&gt;Built on proven foundations&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#built-on-proven-foundations\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;Building a vulnerability scanner that customers will trust with their API credentials demands proven infrastructure. We did not reinvent the wheel here. Instead, we integrated services that have been validated and deployed across Cloudflare for two crucial components of our scanner platform: the scannerГўВҖВҷs control plane and the scannerГўВҖВҷs secrets store.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The scanner&amp;#39;s control plane integrates with &lt;a href=\&quot;https://github.com/temporalio/temporal\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Temporal&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; for Scan Orchestration, on which other internal services at Cloudflare already rely. The complexity of the numerous test plans executed in each Scan is effectively managed by Temporal&amp;#39;s durable execution framework.ГӮВ &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The entire backend is written in Rust, which is widely adopted at Cloudflare for infrastructure services. This lets us reuse internal libraries and share architectural patterns across teams. It also positions our scanner for potential future integration with other Cloudflare systems like FL2 or our test framework &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/20-percent-internet-upgrade/#step-2-testing-and-automated-rollouts\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Flamingo&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; ГўВҖВ“ enabling scenarios where scanning could coordinate more tightly with edge request handling or testing infrastructure.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h4 id=\&quot;credential-security-through-hashicorps-vault-transit-secret-engine\&quot;&gt;Credential security through HashiCorpГўВҖВҷs Vault Transit Secret Engine&lt;/h4&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#credential-security-through-hashicorps-vault-transit-secret-engine\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;Scanning for broken authentication and broken authorization vulnerabilities requires handling API user credentials. Cloudflare takes this responsibility very seriously.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;We ensure that our public API layer has minimal access to unencrypted customer credentials by using HashiCorp&amp;#39;s &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developer.hashicorp.com/vault/docs/secrets/transit\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Vault Transit Secret Engine&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; (TSE) for encryption-as-a-service. Immediately upon submission, credentials are encrypted by TSEГўВҖВ”which handles the encryption but does not store the ciphertextГўВҖВ”and are subsequently stored on Cloudflare infrastructure.ГӮВ &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Our API is not authorized to decrypt this data. Instead, decryption occurs only at the last stage when a TestPlan makes a request to the customer&amp;#39;s infrastructure. Only the Worker executing the test is authorized to request decryption, a restriction we strengthen using strict typing with additional safety rails inside Rust to enforce minimal access to decryption methods.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;We further secure our customersГўВҖВҷ credentials through regular rotation and periodic rewraps using TSE to mitigate risk. This process means we only interact with the new ciphertext, and the original secret is kept unviewable.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h2 id=\&quot;whats-next\&quot;&gt;WhatГўВҖВҷs next?&lt;/h2&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#whats-next\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;We are releasing BOLA vulnerability scanning starting today as an Open Beta for all API Shield customers, and are working on future API threat scans for future release. Via the Cloudflare API, you can trigger scans, manage configuration, and retrieve results programmatically to integrate directly into your &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/learning/serverless/glossary/what-is-ci-cd/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;CI/CD pipelines&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; or security dashboards. For API Shield Customers: check the &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/api-shield/security/vulnerability-scanner/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;developer docs&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; to start scanning your endpoints for BOLA vulnerabilities today.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;We are starting with BOLA vulnerabilities because they are the hardest API vulnerability to solve and the highest risk for our customers. However, this scanning engine is built to be extensible.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;In the near future, we plan to expand the scannerГўВҖВҷs capabilities to cover the most popular of the &lt;a href=\&quot;https://owasp.org/www-project-top-ten/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;OWASP &lt;/u&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;u&gt;Web&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;u&gt; Top 10&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; as well: classic web vulnerabilities like SQL injection (SQLi) and cross-site scripting (XSS). To be notified upon release, &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/lp/security-week/vulnerability-scanner/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;sign up for the waitlist here&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, and youГўВҖВҷll be first to learn when we expand the engine to general web application vulnerabilities.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;],&quot;published_at&quot;:[0,&quot;2026-03-09T14:00+00:00&quot;],&quot;updated_at&quot;:[0,&quot;2026-03-09T17:08:02.333Z&quot;],&quot;feature_image&quot;:[0,&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/5gj8ev1fCNoKxB8UWMxpQW/fdf60a77b33db5ad5455eccd1933ec11/BLOG-3161_1.png&quot;],&quot;tags&quot;:[1,[[0,{&quot;id&quot;:[0,&quot;36Dg2NwTgUHhrlE0FRpSdJ&quot;],&quot;name&quot;:[0,&quot;Application
