vulnerability scanner for APIs&quot;],&quot;description&quot;:[0,&quot;CloudflareГўВҖВҷs new Web and API Vulnerability Scanner helps teams proactively find logic flaws. By using AI to build API call graphs, we identify vulnerabilities that standard defensive tools miss.&quot;],&quot;imgPreview&quot;:[0,&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/4U3CYieZzQmmJN0rvIg6Tx/233e5a30c2400c7956d4d9dc13c67e07/BLOG-3161_OG.png&quot;]}],&quot;publicly_index&quot;:[0,true]}],[0,{&quot;id&quot;:[0,&quot;1b0iJgL57wbfiLHXhEjuwR&quot;],&quot;title&quot;:[0,&quot;Fixing request smuggling vulnerabilities in Pingora OSS deployments&quot;],&quot;slug&quot;:[0,&quot;pingora-oss-smuggling-vulnerabilities&quot;],&quot;excerpt&quot;:[0,&quot;Today weГўВҖВҷre disclosing request smuggling vulnerabilities when our open source Pingora service is deployed as an ingress proxy and how weГўВҖВҷve fixed them in Pingora 0.8.0. &quot;],&quot;featured&quot;:[0,false],&quot;html&quot;:[0,&quot;&lt;p&gt;In December 2025, Cloudflare received reports of HTTP/1.x request smuggling vulnerabilities in the &lt;a href=\&quot;https://github.com/cloudflare/pingora\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Pingora open source&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; framework when Pingora is used to build an ingress proxy. Today we are discussing how these vulnerabilities work and how we patched them in &lt;a href=\&quot;https://github.com/cloudflare/pingora/releases/tag/0.8.0\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Pingora 0.8.0&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The vulnerabilities are &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cve.org/CVERecord?id=CVE-2026-2833\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;CVE-2026-2833&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cve.org/CVERecord?id=CVE-2026-2835\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;CVE-2026-2835&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, and &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cve.org/CVERecord?id=CVE-2026-2836\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;CVE-2026-2836&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. These issues were responsibly reported to us by Rajat Raghav (xclow3n) through our &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/disclosure/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Bug Bounty Program&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;CloudflareГўВҖВҷs CDN and customer traffic were not affected&lt;/b&gt;, our investigation found. &lt;b&gt;No action is needed for Cloudflare customers, and no impact was detected.&lt;/b&gt;ГӮВ &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Due to the architecture of CloudflareГўВҖВҷs network, these vulnerabilities could not be exploited: Pingora is not used as an ingress proxy in CloudflareГўВҖВҷs CDN.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;However, these issues impact standalone Pingora deployments exposed to the Internet, and may enable an attacker to:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Bypass Pingora proxy-layer security controls&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Desync HTTP request/responses with backends for cross-user hijacking attacks (session or credential theft)&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Poison Pingora proxy-layer caches retrieving content from shared backends&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;We have released &lt;a href=\&quot;https://github.com/cloudflare/pingora/releases/tag/0.8.0\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Pingora 0.8.0&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; with fixes and hardening. While Cloudflare customers were not affected, we strongly recommend users of the Pingora framework to &lt;b&gt;upgrade as soon as possible.&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h2 id=\&quot;what-was-the-vulnerability\&quot;&gt;What was the vulnerability?&lt;/h2&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#what-was-the-vulnerability\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;The reports described a few different HTTP/1 attack payloads that could cause desync attacks. Such requests could cause the proxy and backend to disagree about where the request body ends, allowing a second request to be ГўВҖВңsmuggledГўВҖВқ past proxyГўВҖВ‘layer checks. The researcher provided a proof-of-concept to validate how a basic Pingora reverse proxy misinterpreted request body lengths and forwarded those requests to server backends such as Node/Express or uvicorn.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Upon receiving the reports, our engineering team immediately investigated and validated that, as the reporter also confirmed, the Cloudflare CDN itself was not vulnerable. However, the team did also validate that vulnerabilities exist when Pingora acts as the ingress proxy to shared backends.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;By design, the Pingora framework &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/how-we-built-pingora-the-proxy-that-connects-cloudflare-to-the-internet/#design-decisions\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;does allow&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; edge case HTTP requests or responses that are not strictly RFC compliant, because we must accept this sort of traffic for customers with legacy HTTP stacks. But this leniency has limits to avoid exposing Cloudflare itself to vulnerabilities.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;In this case, Pingora had non-RFC-compliant interpretations of request bodies within its HTTP/1 stack that allowed these desync attacks to exist. Pingora deployments within Cloudflare are not directly exposed to ingress traffic, and we found that production traffic that arrived at Pingora services were not subject to these misinterpretations. Thus, the attacks were not exploitable on Cloudflare traffic itself, unlike a &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/resolving-a-request-smuggling-vulnerability-in-pingora/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;previous Pingora smuggling vulnerability&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; disclosed in May 2025.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;WeГўВҖВҷll explain, case-by-case, how these attack payloads worked.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;1-premature-upgrade-without-101-handshake\&quot;&gt;1. Premature upgrade without 101 handshake&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#1-premature-upgrade-without-101-handshake\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;The first report showed that a request with an &lt;code&gt;Upgrade&lt;/code&gt; header value would cause Pingora to pass through subsequent bytes on the HTTP connection immediately, before the backend had accepted an upgrade (by returning &lt;code&gt;101 Switching Protocols&lt;/code&gt;). The attacker could thus pipeline a second HTTP request after the upgrade request on the same connection:&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-Rust\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-Rust\&quot;&gt;GET / HTTP/1.1\nHost: example.com\nUpgrade: foo\n\n\nGET /admin HTTP/1.1\nHost: example.com&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            &lt;p&gt;Pingora would parse only the initial request, then treat the remaining buffered bytes as the ГўВҖВңupgradedГўВҖВқ stream and forward them directly to the backend in a ГўВҖВңpassthroughГўВҖВқ mode &lt;a href=\&quot;https://github.com/cloudflare/pingora/blob/ef017ceb01962063addbacdab2a4fd2700039db5/pingora-core/src/protocols/http/v1/server.rs#L797\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;due to the Upgrade header&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; (until the response &lt;a href=\&quot;https://github.com/cloudflare/pingora/blob/ef017ceb01962063addbacdab2a4fd2700039db5/pingora-core/src/protocols/http/v1/server.rs#L523\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;was received&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;).&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;This is not at all how the HTTP/1.1 Upgrade process per &lt;a href=\&quot;https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc9110#field.upgrade\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;RFC 9110&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; is intended to work. The subsequent bytes should &lt;i&gt;only&lt;/i&gt; be interpreted as part of an upgraded stream if a &lt;code&gt;101 Switching Protocols&lt;/code&gt; header is received, and if a &lt;code&gt;200 OK&lt;/code&gt; response is received instead, the subsequent bytes should continue to be interpreted as HTTP.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/2IYHyGkABpNA0e09wiiGpY/4f51ea330c2d266260f6361dd9d64d79/image4.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1755\&quot; height=\&quot;1125\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;sup&gt;&lt;i&gt;An attacker that sends an Upgrade request, then pipelines a partial HTTP request may cause a desync attack. Pingora will incorrectly interpret both as the same upgraded request, even if the backend server declines the upgrade with a 200.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Via the improper pass-through, a Pingora deployment that received a non-101 response could still forward the second partial HTTP request to the upstream as-is, bypassing any Pingora userГўВҖВ‘defined ACL-handling or WAF logic, and poison the connection to the upstream so that a subsequent request from a different user could improperly receive the &lt;code&gt;/admin&lt;/code&gt; response.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/oIwatu6gaMoJHCCs95sFN/8ea94ee8f04be6f7f00474168b382180/image3.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1755\&quot; height=\&quot;648\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;sup&gt;&lt;i&gt;After the attack payload, Pingora and the backend server are now ГўВҖВңdesynced.ГўВҖВқ The backend server will wait until it thinks the rest of the partial /attack request header that Pingora forwarded is complete. When Pingora forwards a different userГўВҖВҷs request, the two headers are combined from the backend serverГўВҖВҷs perspective, and the attacker has now poisoned the other userГўВҖВҷs response.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;WeГўВҖВҷve since &lt;a href=\&quot;https://github.com/cloudflare/pingora/commit/824bdeefc61e121cc8861de1b35e8e8f39026ecd\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;patched&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; Pingora to switch the interpretation of subsequent bytes only once the upstream responds with &lt;code&gt;101 Switching Protocols&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;We verified Cloudflare was &lt;b&gt;not affected&lt;/b&gt; for two reasons:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ol&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;The ingress CDN proxies do not have this improper behavior.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;The clients to our internal Pingora services do not attempt to &lt;a href=\&quot;https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTTP_pipelining\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;pipeline&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; HTTP/1 requests. Furthermore, the Pingora service these clients talk directly with disables keep-alive on these &lt;code&gt;Upgrade&lt;/code&gt; requests by injecting a &lt;code&gt;Connection: close&lt;/code&gt; header; this prevents additional requests that would be sent ГўВҖВ” and subsequently smuggled ГўВҖВ” over the same connection.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;2-http-1-0-close-delimiting-and-transfer-encoding\&quot;&gt;2. HTTP/1.0, close-delimiting, and transfer-encoding&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#2-http-1-0-close-delimiting-and-transfer-encoding\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;The reporter also demonstrated what &lt;i&gt;appeared&lt;/i&gt; to be a more classic ГўВҖВңCL.TEГўВҖВқ desync-type attack, where the Pingora proxy would use Content-Length as framing while the backend would use Transfer-Encoding as framing:&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-Rust\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-Rust\&quot;&gt;GET / HTTP/1.0\nHost: example.com\nConnection: keep-alive\nTransfer-Encoding: identity, chunked\nContent-Length: 29\n\n0\n\nGET /admin HTTP/1.1\nX:\n&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            &lt;p&gt;In the reporterГўВҖВҷs example, Pingora would treat all subsequent bytes after the first GET / request header as part of that requestГўВҖВҷs body, but the node.js backend server would interpret the body as chunked and ending at the zero-length chunk. There are actually a few things going on here:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ol&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;PingoraГўВҖВҷs chunked encoding recognition was quite barebones (only checking for whether &lt;code&gt;Transfer-Encoding&lt;/code&gt; was ГўВҖВң&lt;a href=\&quot;https://github.com/cloudflare/pingora/blob/9ac75d0356f449d26097e08bf49af14de6271727/pingora-core/src/protocols/http/v1/common.rs#L146\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;chunked&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;ГўВҖВқ) and assumed that there could only be one encoding or &lt;code&gt;Transfer-Encoding&lt;/code&gt; header. But the RFC only &lt;a href=\&quot;https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc9112#section-6.3-2.4.1\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;mandates&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; that the &lt;i&gt;final&lt;/i&gt; encoding must be &lt;code&gt;chunked&lt;/code&gt; to apply chunked framing. So per RFC, this request should have a chunked message body (if it were not HTTP/1.0 ГўВҖВ” more on that below).&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Pingora was &lt;i&gt;also &lt;/i&gt;not actually using the &lt;code&gt;Content-Length&lt;/code&gt; (because the Transfer-Encoding overrode the Content-Length &lt;a href=\&quot;https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc9112#section-6.3-2.3\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;per RFC&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;). Because of the unrecognized Transfer-Encoding and the HTTP/1.0 version, the request body was &lt;a href=\&quot;https://github.com/cloudflare/pingora/blob/ef017ceb01962063addbacdab2a4fd2700039db5/pingora-core/src/protocols/http/v1/server.rs#L817\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;instead treated as close-delimited&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; (which means that the response bodyГўВҖВҷs end is marked by closure of the underlying transport connection). An absence of framing headers would also trigger the same misinterpretation on HTTP/1.0. Although response bodies are allowed to be close-delimited, request bodies are &lt;i&gt;never&lt;/i&gt; close-delimited. In fact, this clarification is now explicitly called out as a separate note in &lt;a href=\&quot;https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc9112#section-6.3-4.1\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;RFC 9112&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;This is an HTTP/1.0 request that &lt;a href=\&quot;https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc9112#appendix-C.2.3-1\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;did not define&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; Transfer-Encoding. The RFC &lt;a href=\&quot;https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc9112#section-6.1-16\&quot;&gt;mandates&lt;/a&gt; that HTTP/1.0 requests containing Transfer-Encoding must ГўВҖВңtreat the message as if the framing is faultyГўВҖВқ and close the connection. Parsers such as the ones in nginx and hyper just reject these requests to avoid ambiguous framing.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/1jLbMNafmF96toxAPxj2Cm/8561b96a56dc0fc654476e33d0f34888/image2.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1755\&quot; height=\&quot;1082\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;sup&gt;&lt;i&gt;When an attacker pipelines a partial HTTP request header after the HTTP/1.0 + Transfer-Encoding request, Pingora would incorrectly interpret that partial header as part of the same request, rather than as a distinct request. This enables the same kind of desync attack as described in the premature Upgrade example.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;This spoke to a more fundamental misreading of the RFC particularly in terms of response vs. request message framing. WeГўВҖВҷve since fixed the improper &lt;a href=\&quot;https://github.com/cloudflare/pingora/commit/7f7166d62fa916b9f11b2eb8f9e3c4999e8b9023\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;multiple Transfer-Encoding parsing&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, adhere strictly to the request length guidelines such that HTTP request bodies can &lt;a href=\&quot;https://github.com/cloudflare/pingora/commit/40c3c1e9a43a86b38adeab8da7a2f6eba68b83ad\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;never be considered close-delimited&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, and reject &lt;a href=\&quot;https://github.com/cloudflare/pingora/commit/fc904c0d2c679be522de84729ec73f0bd344963d\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;invalid Content-Length&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href=\&quot;https://github.com/cloudflare/pingora/commit/87e2e2fb37edf9be33e3b1d04726293ae6bf2052\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;HTTP/1.0 + Transfer-Encoding&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; request messages. Further protections weГўВҖВҷve added include &lt;a href=\&quot;https://github.com/cloudflare/pingora/commit/d3d2cf5ef4eca1e5d327fe282ec4b4ee474350c6\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;rejecting&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; &lt;a href=\&quot;https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc9110#name-connect\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;CONNECT&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; requests by default because the HTTP proxy logic doesnГўВҖВҷt currently treat CONNECT as special for the purposes of CONNECT upgrade proxying, and these requests have special &lt;a href=\&quot;https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc9112#section-6.3-2.2\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;message framing rules&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. (Note that incoming CONNECT requests are &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/fundamentals/concepts/traffic-flow-cloudflare/#cloudflares-network\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;rejected&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; by the Cloudflare CDN.)&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;When we investigated and instrumented our services internally, we found no requests arriving at our Pingora services that would have been misinterpreted. We found that downstream proxy layers in the CDN would forward as HTTP/1.1 only, reject ambiguous framing such as invalid Content-Length, and only forward a single &lt;code&gt;Transfer-Encoding: chunked&lt;/code&gt; header for chunked requests.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;3-cache-key-construction\&quot;&gt;3. Cache key construction&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#3-cache-key-construction\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;The researcher also reported one other cache poisoning vulnerability regarding default &lt;code&gt;CacheKey&lt;/code&gt; construction. The &lt;a href=\&quot;https://github.com/cloudflare/pingora/blob/ef017ceb01962063addbacdab2a4fd2700039db5/pingora-cache/src/key.rs#L218\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;naive default implementation&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; factored in only the URI path (without other factors such as host header or upstream server HTTP scheme), which meant different hosts using the same HTTP path could collide and poison each otherГўВҖВҷs cache.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;This would affect users of the alpha proxy caching feature who chose to use the default &lt;code&gt;CacheKey&lt;/code&gt; implementation. We have since &lt;a href=\&quot;https://github.com/cloudflare/pingora/commit/257b59ada28ed6cac039f67d0b71f414efa0ab6e\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;removed that default&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, because while using something like HTTP scheme + host + URI makes sense for many applications, we want users to be careful when constructing their cache keys for themselves. If their proxy logic will conditionally adjust the URI or method on the upstream request, for example, that logic likely also must be factored into the cache key scheme to avoid poisoning.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Internally, CloudflareГўВҖВҷs &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/cache/how-to/cache-keys/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;default cache key&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; uses a number of factors to prevent cache key poisoning, and never made use of the previously provided default.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h2 id=\&quot;recommendation\&quot;&gt;Recommendation&lt;/h2&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#recommendation\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;If you use Pingora as a proxy, upgrade to &lt;a href=\&quot;https://github.com/cloudflare/pingora/releases/tag/0.8.0\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Pingora 0.8.0&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; at your earliest convenience.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;We apologize for the impact this vulnerability may have had on Pingora users. As Pingora earns its place as critical Internet infrastructure beyond Cloudflare, we believe itГўВҖВҷs important for the framework to promote use of strict RFC compliance by default and will continue this effort. Very few users of the framework should have to deal with the same ГўВҖВңwild InternetГўВҖВқ that Cloudflare does. Our intention is that stricter adherence to the latest RFC standards by default will harden security for Pingora users and move the Internet as a whole toward best practices.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h2 id=\&quot;disclosure-and-response-timeline\&quot;&gt;Disclosure and response timeline&lt;/h2&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#disclosure-and-response-timeline\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;- 2025ГўВҖВ‘12ГўВҖВ‘02: UpgradeГўВҖВ‘based smuggling reported via bug bounty.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;- 2026ГўВҖВ‘01ГўВҖВ‘13: TransferГўВҖВ‘Encoding / HTTP/1.0 parsing issues reported.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;- 2026-01-18: Default cache key construction issue reported.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;- 2026ГўВҖВ‘01ГўВҖВ‘29 to 2026ГўВҖВ‘02ГўВҖВ‘13: Fixes validated with the reporter. Work on more RFC-compliance checks continues.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;- 2026-02-25: Cache key default removal and additional RFC checks validated with researcher.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;- 2026ГўВҖВ‘03-02: Pingora 0.8.0 released.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;- 2026-03-04: CVE advisories published.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h2 id=\&quot;acknowledgements\&quot;&gt;Acknowledgements&lt;/h2&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#acknowledgements\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;We thank Rajat Raghav (xclow3n) for the report, detailed reproductions, and verification of the fixes through our bug bounty program. If you&amp;apos;re looking for a new career direction, check out &lt;a target=&#39;_blank&#39; href=&#39;http://www.cloudflare.com/careers&#39; rel=&#39;noreferrer&#39;&gt;our open positions&lt;/a&gt;.&quot;]}" ssr client="load" opts="{&quot;name&quot;:&quot;Post&quot;,&quot;value&quot;:true}" await-children><main id="post" class="flex flex-row flex-wrap items-center justify-center pt2 pt4-l"><article class="post-full mw-100 ph3 ph0-l fs-20px"><h1 class="f6 f7-l fw4 gray1 pt1 pt3-l mb1">Announcing Cloudflare Account Abuse Protection: prevent fraudulent attacks from bots and humans</h1><p class="f3 fw5 gray5 db di-l mt2">2026-03-12</p><ul class="author-lists flex pl0 mt4"><li class="list flex items-center pr2 mb1-ns"><a href="/author/jin-hee-lee/" class="static-avatar pr1"><img class="author-profile-image br-100 mr2" src="https://blog.cloudflare.com/cdn-cgi/image/format=auto,dpr=3,width=64,height=64,gravity=face,fit=crop,zoom=0.5/https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/47LTVC3FaSVzkAumTWfFIi/4424dfc2819cbc4a8fff6b72ce93047e/Jin-Hee_Lee.jpg" alt="Jin-Hee Lee" width="62" height="62"/></a><div class="author-name-tooltip"><a href="/author/jin-hee-lee/" class="fw4 f3 no-underline black mr3">Jin-Hee Lee</a></div></li></ul><section class="post-full-content"><div class="mb2 gray5">7 min read</div><img class="mr2" src="https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/1xUHwg1io7QsO9sswX7GpD/2066c94abed41c9b6e4397173955cae7/image3.png" alt=""/><div class="post-content lh-copy gray1"><p>Today, Cloudflare is introducing a new suite of fraud prevention capabilities designed to stop account abuse before it starts. We&#39;ve spent years empowering Cloudflare customers to protect their applications from automated attacks, but the threat landscape has evolved. The industrialization of hybrid automated-and-human abuse presents a complex security challenge to website owners. Consider, for instance, a single account thatГўВҖВҷs accessed from New York, London, and San Francisco in the same five minutes. The core question in this case is not ГўВҖВңIs this automated?ГўВҖВқ but rather ГўВҖВңIs this authentic?ГўВҖВқГӮВ </p><p><b>Website owners need the tools to stop abuse on their website, no matter who itГўВҖВҷs coming from</b>.</p><p>During our Birthday Week in 2024, we gifted <a href="https://developers.cloudflare.com/waf/detections/leaked-credentials/"><u>leaked credentials detection</u></a> to all customers, including everyone on a Free plan. Since then, we&#39;ve added <a href="https://developers.cloudflare.com/bots/additional-configurations/detection-ids/#account-takeover-detections"><u>account takeover detection IDs</u></a> as part of our <a href="https://www.cloudflare.com/application-services/products/bot-management/"><u>bot management solution</u></a> to help identify bots attacking your login pages.ГӮВ </p><p>Now, weГўВҖВҷre combining these powerful tools with new ones. <b>Disposable email check</b> and <b>email risk </b>help you enforce security preferences for users who sign up with throwaway email addresses, a common tactic for fake account creation and promotion abuse, or whose emails are deemed risky based on email patterns and infrastructure. WeГўВҖВҷre also thrilled to introduce <b>Hashed User IDs</b> ГўВҖВ” per-domain identifiers generated by cryptographically hashing usernames ГўВҖВ” that give customers better insight into suspicious account activity and greater ability to mitigate potentially fraudulent traffic, without compromising end user privacy.</p><p><b>The new capabilities weГўВҖВҷre announcing today go beyond automation, identifying abusive behavior and risky identities among human users </b><b><i>and</i></b><b> bots. </b><a href="https://developers.cloudflare.com/bots/account-abuse-protection/"><u>Account Abuse Protection</u></a> is available in Early Access, and any Bot Management Enterprise customer can use these features at no additional cost for a limited period, until the general availability of Cloudflare Fraud Prevention later this year. If you want to learn more about this Early Access capability, <a href="https://www.cloudflare.com/lp/account-abuse-protection/"><u>sign up here</u></a>.</p>
    <div class="flex anchor relative">
      <h3 id="leaked-credentials-make-logins-all-too-vulnerable">Leaked credentials make logins all too vulnerable</h3>
      <a href="#leaked-credentials-make-logins-all-too-vulnerable" aria-hidden="true" class="relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5">
        <svg width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path fill="currentcolor" d="m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z"></path></svg>
      </a>
    </div>
    <p>The barrier to entry for fraudulent behavior is dangerously low, especially with the availability of massive datasets and access to automated tools that commit account fraud at scale. Website owners arenГўВҖВҷt just dealing with individual hackers, but industrialized fraud. Last year, we highlighted how <a href="https://blog.cloudflare.com/password-reuse-rampant-half-user-logins-compromised/"><b><u>41% of logins across our network use leaked credentials</u></b></a>. This number has only grown following the exposure of a database holding <a href="https://cybernews.com/security/billions-credentials-exposed-infostealers-data-leak/"><u>16 billion records</u></a>, and multiple high-profile breaches have since come to light.ГӮВ </p><p>WhatГўВҖВҷs more, users reuse passwords across multiple platforms, meaning a single leak from years ago can still unlock a high-value retail or even a bank account today. Our <a href="https://developers.cloudflare.com/waf/detections/leaked-credentials/#leaked-credentials-fields"><u>leaked credential check</u></a> is a free feature that checks whether a password has been leaked in a known data breach of another service or application on the Internet. This is a privacy-preserving credential checking service that helps protect our users from compromised credentials, meaning Cloudflare performs these checks without accessing or storing plaintext end user passwords. <a href="https://blog.cloudflare.com/helping-keep-customers-safe-with-leaked-password-notification/#how-does-cloudflare-check-for-leaked-credentials"><u>Passwords are hashed ГўВҖВ” i.e., converted into a random string of characters using a cryptographic algorithm ГўВҖВ” for the purpose of comparing them against a database of leaked credentials.</u></a> If you havenГўВҖВҷt already turned on our <a href="https://developers.cloudflare.com/waf/detections/leaked-credentials/#leaked-credentials-fields"><u>leaked credential check</u></a>, enable it now to keep your accounts safe from easy hacks!</p><p>Access to a large database of leaked credentials is only useful if an attacker can cycle through them quickly across many sites to identify which accounts are still vulnerable due to password reuse. In our Black Friday analysis in 2024, we observed that more than <a href="https://blog.cloudflare.com/grinch-bot-2024/"><b><u>60% of traffic to login pages across our network was automated</u></b></a>. ThatГўВҖВҷs a lot of bots trying to break in.</p><p>To help customers protect their login endpoints from constant bombardment, we added <a href="https://www.cloudflare.com/learning/access-management/account-takeover/"><u>account takeover</u></a> <a href="https://developers.cloudflare.com/bots/additional-configurations/detection-ids/account-takeover-detections/"><u>(ATO)-specific detections</u></a> to highlight suspicious traffic patterns. This is part of our recent focus on <a href="https://blog.cloudflare.com/per-customer-bot-defenses/"><u>per-customer detections</u></a>, in which we provide behavioral anomaly detection unique to each bot management customer. Today, bot management customers can see and mitigate attempted ATO attacks in their login requests directly on the Security analytics dashboard.</p>
          <figure class="kg-card kg-image-card">
          <Image src="https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/3f2nQ5wBVQ2WqiKGsjVWJe/3c1011ced84e46f65938f32c88035de9/image5.png" alt="" class="kg-image" width="1334" height="492" loading="lazy"/>
          </figure><p><sup><i>In the card on the left within the Security analytics dashboard, you can view and address attempted account takeover attacks.</i></sup></p><p>In the last week, our ATO detections combined caught an average of <b>6.9 billion suspicious login attempts</b> daily, across our network. These ATO detections, along with the many other detection mechanisms in our bot management solution, create a <i>layered defense</i> against ATO and other malicious automated attacks.</p>
    <div class="flex anchor relative">
      <h3 id="from-automation-to-intent-and-identity">From automation to intent and identity</h3>
      <a href="#from-automation-to-intent-and-identity" aria-hidden="true" class="relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5">
        <svg width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path fill="currentcolor" d="m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z"></path></svg>
      </a>
    </div>
    <p>To discern automation, or to discern intent and identity? That is the question. Our answer: yes and yes, as both are critical layers of a robust security posture. Attackers now operate at a scale previously reserved for enterprise services: they leverage massive credential leaks, use human-powered fraud farms to spoof devices and locations, and create synthetic identities to maintain thousands ГўВҖВ” even millions ГўВҖВ” of fake accounts for promotion and platform abuse. A human being with automated tools could be draining accounts, abusing promotions, committing payment fraud, or all of the above.</p><p>Beyond that, automation is accessible like never before, particularly as users become better acquainted with using <a href="https://www.cloudflare.com/learning/ai/what-is-agentic-ai/"><u>AI agents</u></a> and even long-standing, ГўВҖВңtraditionalГўВҖВқ browsers move toward having agentic capabilities by default. Whether itГўВҖВҷs a lone actor using an AI agent or a coordinated fraud campaign, the threat isnГўВҖВҷt as simple as a single script ГўВҖВ” it can involve human intent, with automated execution.</p><p>Consider the following scenarios weГўВҖВҷve heard from our customers:</p><ul><li><p>We have 1,000 new users this month, but more than half of them are fake identities who benefit from a free trial, then disappear.</p></li><li><p>The attacker logged in with the correct password, so how do I know that it isnГўВҖВҷt the real user?</p></li><li><p>This entity is acting at human pace, and they are draining accounts.</p></li></ul><p>These problems can&#39;t be solved by <i>only</i> assessing automation; they require checking for authenticity and integrity. This is the gap that our dedicated fraud prevention capabilities address.</p>
    <div class="flex anchor relative">
      <h3 id="assessing-suspicious-emails">Assessing suspicious emails</h3>
      <a href="#assessing-suspicious-emails" aria-hidden="true" class="relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5">
        <svg width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path fill="currentcolor" d="m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z"></path></svg>
      </a>
    </div>
    <p>LetГўВҖВҷs start by assessing the earliest point of potential account abuse: account creation. Fake or bulk account creation is one of the biggest topics in conversations about website fraud, as it can open the door for attackers to access an application ГўВҖВ” or even an entire business model.ГӮВ </p><p>Cloudflare is giving customers the tools to assess suspicious account creation at the source in two ways:</p><ol><li><p><b>Disposable email check</b>: Detect when users sign up with disposable, or throwaway, email addresses commonly used for promotion abuse and fake account creation. These disposable email services allow attackers to spin up thousands of &quot;unique&quot; accounts without maintaining real infrastructure, particularly unauthenticated disposable emails that provide instant access without account creation or free unlimited email aliases. Customers can use this binary field as they build rules to enforce security preferences, choosing to block all disposable emails outright, or perhaps issuing a <a href="https://developers.cloudflare.com/cloudflare-challenges/challenge-types/"><u>challenge</u></a> to anyone attempting to create an account with a disposable email.
</p>
          <figure class="kg-card kg-image-card">
          <Image src="https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/3PQC7PqKWrhl5c4OCXu5Ha/9340e3b49cc396ca5f5d01d34fd529d5/image2.png" alt="" class="kg-image" width="1638" height="344" loading="lazy"/>
          </figure></li><li><p><b>Email risk:</b> Cloudflare analyzes email patterns and infrastructure to provide risk tiers (low, medium, high) that customers can use in security rules. We know that not all email addresses are created equal; an address with the format <code><a href="/cdn-cgi/l/email-protection" class="__cf_email__" data-cfemail="c1a7a8b3b2b5afa0aca4efada0b2b5afa0aca481aaafaeb6afa5aeaca0a8afefa2aeac">[email&#160;protected]</a></code> carries different risk characteristics than <code><a href="/cdn-cgi/l/email-protection" class="__cf_email__" data-cfemail="c6beadf1b7ffabf4b686a8a3b1a2a9aba7afa8e8bebfbc">[email&#160;protected]</a></code>. Email risk tiers allow customers to express their tolerance for risk and friction at the point of account creation.ГӮВ </p></li></ol><p>Both disposable email check and email risk are now available in security analytics and security rules, equipping website owners to protect their account creation flow. These detections address a fundamental problem: by the time an account is committing abuse, it&#39;s already too late. The website owner has already paid acquisition costs, the fraudulent user has consumed promotional credits, and remediation requires manual review. Mitigating suspicious emails means adding the appropriate friction at signup ГўВҖВ” the moment it matters most.</p>
    <div class="flex anchor relative">
      <h3 id="introducing-hashed-user-ids">Introducing Hashed User IDs</h3>
      <a href="#introducing-hashed-user-ids" aria-hidden="true" class="relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5">
        <svg width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path fill="currentcolor" d="m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z"></path></svg>
      </a>
    </div>
    <p>Understanding patterns of abuse requires <i>visibility</i>: not only into the network, but of account activity. Traditionally, security has meant looking through the lens of IPs and isolated HTTP requests to spot automated activity, but website owners arenГўВҖВҷt just thinking in terms of network signals; they are also considering their users and known accounts. ThatГўВҖВҷs why weГўВҖВҷre expanding our mitigation toolbox to match the way applications are actually structured, focusing on user-based detection of fraudulent activity.</p><p>Attackers can effortlessly rotate IPs to hide their tracks. But forcing them to repeatedly generate new, credible accounts introduces massive friction, especially when combined with account creation protections. When we look past the network layer and map fraudulent actions to a given compromised or abusive account, we can spot targeted behavior tied to a single, persistent actor and put a stop to the abuse. In this way, weГўВҖВҷre shifting the defense strategy to the account level, instead of playing whack-a-mole with rotating IP addresses and residential proxies. This means that <b>our customers can mitigate abusive behavior based on the way </b><b><i>their</i></b><b> applications separate identity</b>.</p><p>To arm website owners with this capability, Cloudflare is releasing a <a href="https://developers.cloudflare.com/bots/account-abuse-protection/#user-id"><b><u>Hashed User ID</u></b></a> that customers can use in <a href="https://developers.cloudflare.com/waf/analytics/security-analytics/"><u>Security analytics</u></a>, <a href="https://developers.cloudflare.com/waf/custom-rules/"><u>Security rules</u></a>, and <a href="https://developers.cloudflare.com/rules/transform/managed-transforms/reference/"><u>Managed Transforms</u></a>. User IDs are per-domain, cryptographically hashed versions of the values in the username field, and each user ID is an encrypted, unique, and stable identifier generated for a given username on a customer application. <b>Importantly, the actual username is not logged or stored by Cloudflare as part of this service.</b> As with leaked credentials check and ATO detections, which identify login traffic and then encrypt credentials for comparison, we are prioritizing end user privacy while empowering our customers to take action against fraudulent behavior.</p><p>With access to Hashed User IDs, website owners can:</p><ul><li><p>See top users: Which accounts have the most activity?</p></li><li><p>See when a unique user logs in from a country they usually donГўВҖВҷt ГўВҖВ” or multiple countries in one day!</p></li><li><p>Mitigate traffic based on unique user, such as blocking a user with historically suspicious activity.</p></li><li><p>Combine fields to see when accounts are being targeted with leaked credentials.</p></li><li><p>See what network patterns or signals are associated with unique users.</p></li></ul>
          <figure class="kg-card kg-image-card">
          <Image src="https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/3f7Jm4HnngjYEmKG8QSiyC/2ae3543f0cd0eb072a0c4c2bb12c4436/image4.png" alt="" class="kg-image" width="1110" height="736" loading="lazy"/>
          </figure><p><sup><i>The expanded view of a single Hashed User ID within the Security analytics dashboard, showing the activity details of that unique user, including their login location and their browser.ГӮВ </i></sup></p><p>This user-level visibility transforms how website owners can investigate and mitigate traffic. Instead of examining individual requests in isolation, our customers can see the full picture of how attackers are targeting and hiding among legitimate users.</p>
    <div class="flex anchor relative">
      <h3 id="take-the-next-step-in-account-protection-today">Take the next step in account protection today</h3>
      <a href="#take-the-next-step-in-account-protection-today" aria-hidden="true" class="relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5">
        <svg width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path fill="currentcolor" d="m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z"></path></svg>
      </a>
    </div>
    <p>If you want to learn more about this Early Access capability, <a href="https://www.cloudflare.com/lp/account-abuse-protection/"><u>sign up here</u></a>. All Bot Management Enterprise customers are eligible to add these new Account Abuse Protection features today, and weГўВҖВҷd love to open the conversation with any and all <a href="https://www.cloudflare.com/lp/account-abuse-protection"><u>prospective Bot Management customers</u></a>.</p><p>While bot detections will continue to answer the question of automation and intent, fraud detections delve into the question of authenticity. Together, they give website owners comprehensive tools to fight against the full spectrum of account abuse. This suite is one step in our ongoing investment to protect the entire user journey ГўВҖВ” from account creation and login to secure checkouts and the integrity of every interaction.</p></div></section><section class="post-full-content flex flex-row flex-wrap mw7 center mb4"><div class="post-content lh-copy w-100 gray1 bt b--gray8 pt4">Cloudflare's connectivity cloud protects <a target='_blank' href='https://www.cloudflare.com/network-services/' rel='noreferrer'>entire corporate networks</a>, helps customers build <a target='_blank' href='https://workers.cloudflare.com/' rel='noreferrer'>Internet-scale applications efficiently</a>, accelerates any <a target='_blank' href='https://www.cloudflare.com/performance/accelerate-internet-applications/' rel='noreferrer'>website or Internet application</a>, <a target='_blank' href='https://www.cloudflare.com/ddos/' rel='noreferrer'>wards off DDoS attacks</a>, keeps <a target='_blank' href='https://www.cloudflare.com/application-security/' rel='noreferrer'>hackers at bay</a>, and can help you on <a target='_blank' href='https://www.cloudflare.com/products/zero-trust/' rel='noreferrer'>your journey to Zero Trust</a>.<br/><br/>Visit <a target='_blank' href='https://one.one.one.one/' rel='noreferrer'>1.1.1.1</a> from any device to get started with our free app that makes your Internet faster and safer.<br/><br/>To learn more about our mission to help build a better Internet, <a target='_blank' href='https://www.cloudflare.com/learning/what-is-cloudflare/' rel='noreferrer'>start here</a>.
